@HAsian Women's Online Championship, Online<br>August 23rd-26th, 2021
WFM Vyanla Punsalan scored 4/9 and Emily Gan scored 3/9 in the <a href="https://chess-results.com/tnr574231.aspx?lan=1&art=4&flag=30">Asian Women's Online Championship</a>.

@snippet
@HFIDE Online Olympiad, Online<br>August 27-29th, 2021
NZL played in <a href="https://chess-results.com/tnr575555.aspx?lan=1&art=0&flag=30">Division 3A</a>.
<br>Here is the 9 round 10 team, round-robin <a href="https://chess-results.com/tnr575555.aspx?lan=1&art=14&flag=30">schedule</a>. Note than NZ time is 12 hours ahead of UTC, so our games are
quite conveniently scheduled for 8pm, 9pm and 10pm on Friday, Saturday and Sunday.
<br>The player pairings appear <a href="https://chess-results.com/tnr575555.aspx?lan=1&art=2&flag=30">here</a> immediately before each round.
</p><p>
Our team is ably captained by the tireless Timothy Ha and comprises Allen Fan, Dylan Piwari, Sophia Feng, Yolanda Chang,
Oliver Picken, Isabelle Ning, Felix Xie, Ryan Winter, Anya Thurner, Emily Gan, Alex Coates and Ritika Joseph.
</p><p>
Timothy has provided links for following the NZL action as follows;
Here is a <a href="downloads/2021_FIDE_Online_Olympiad_NZL.pgn">final PGN of New Zealand games</a> and here are our final results;
</p><p>

@snippet
@HFIDE Cadets and Youth Rapid World Cup, Online<br>August 1st - August 31st, 2021
The first stage of the tournament is complete. The following sections included NZ players.
</p><p>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565782.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Open U10</a>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565783.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Open U12</a>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565785.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Open U16</a>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565786.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Open U18</a>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565787.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Girls U10</a>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565788.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Girls U12</a>
<a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565789.aspx?lan=1&art=4&fedb=NZL&flag=30">Girls U14</a>
</p><p>
Here is a <a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr565789.aspx?lan=1&art=25&fedb=NZL&flag=30">NZL overview</a> (kind of - the normally reliable chess-results website is a little confusing on this occasion). 
</p><p>
Five different age groups (U10, U12, U14, U16, U18) and two sections, Open and Girls. Participants
must have been age qualified on January 1st 2021. So for example U10 participants must have been
under 10, i.e. had not yet reached their 10th birthday, at the start of this calendar year. NZCF
may select up to three participants in each group and section, so up to 3 x 5 x 2 = 30 players in
total.
</p><p>
The tournament has two stages, 10 round Swiss tournaments in the first stage (through
August 20th), then a knockout stage for a limited number of qualifying players.
</p><p>
More details are available on the FIDE Calendar <a href="https://www.fide.com/calendar/51523">here</a>.

@HSummit Junior Rapid, Auckland<br>August 8th 2021
Open
<br>1st Justin Wang 6/6
<br>2nd Francisco Nascimento 5/6
<br>3rd= Victor Coen, William Liu, Brillion Lau, Sophia Feng 4.5/6
<br>Best U1300 Annie Yue 4/6
<br>Best U1200 Pranav Shenoy 4/6
</p><p>
U1000
<br>1st Richard Liu 7/7 
<br>2nd= Bosco Jin, Sam Lin, Kyan Zhang 6/7
<br>Best U500 1st Claire Gu 5/7, 2nd Isaac Gu 5/7
<br>Best U200 1st Jeremy Xu 5/7, 2nd Luna Xu 4.5/7
</p><p>
Venue: Lyell Creek Lounge, Alexandra Park, Greenlane
<br>Two divisions: Open (FIDE and NZCF rapid rated) and U1000 (NZCF rapid rated).
<br>Format: Six-round Swiss, 15mins+5 secs.
<br>Organised by Summit Chess Club, contact Ying Wang, Email: <a href="mailto:ywang@outlook.co.nz">ywang@outlook.co.nz</a>.
<a href="tournaments/misc/2021/Summit Junior Rapid/wwwAugust 8 U1000">U1000</a>.
<br>Full results on Vega: <a href="tournaments/misc/2021/Summit Junior Rapid/wwwAugust 8 Open">Open</a>,
<a href="tournaments/misc/2021/Summit Junior Rapid/wwwAugust 8 U1000">U1000</a>.
<br>Entry form available <a href="downloads/Summit Junior Rapid 2021.pdf">here</a>.

@HNorthland Open, Whangarei<br>July 31st-August 1st 2021
Results will hopefully be available in due course.
</p><p>
Venue: Henderson Reeves, 96 Bank Street, Whangarei Central.
<br>Six-round Swiss, 30 minutes per player per game, 3 games per afternoon from 12.30pm
<br>Free entry, koha welcomed to buy more chess sets for Whangarei Chess Club.
<br>Online entry via the <a href=https://whangareichess.wordpress.com/">club website</a>.

@snippet
@HPoppies Bookshop Chess Challenge, Howick<br>July 24th 2021
Venue: Poppies Bookshop, 83 Picton St, Howick.
<br>A six game blitz match between NZ rapid champion Felix Xie and CM Oliver Picken. This promotional event
celebrates FIDE International Chess Day. Co-sponsored by the Howick Business Association and Howick-Pakuranga
Chess Club.
<br>Organiser Paul Spiller.
<br>Felix Xie won the last game to win a close and exciting match, final score 3.5-2.5.

@grid
images/2021/poppies match.jpg
Oliver Picken and Felix Xie
Noses to the window as Oliver Picken (Black) faces Felix Xie under the watchful eye of Dr Tony Booth

@snippet
@HGeorge Trundle, Auckland<br>July 10th-18th 2021
Masters
<br>1st	IM Paul Garbett 7/9	
<br>2nd	FM Alphaeus Ang 6.5/9
<br>3rd= FM Mike Steadman, CM David Cilia Vincenti 5.5/9
</p><p>
Qualifiers			
<br>1st CM Richard Meng 7.5/9
<br>2nd CM Alex Nagorski 6/9
<br>3rd= CM Hilton Bennett, FM Robert Gibbons 5.5/9
</p><p>
Reserves			
<br>1st	Aaron Ziwen Wang 8/9	
<br>2nd Zachary Yu 6.5/9
<br>3rd= Simon Lyall, WCM Nadia Braganza 5/9
</p><p>
Talents			
<br>1st	Lucas Barnett-Harris 7/9	
<br>2nd= Emily Gan, David Junyang Zhu 6.5/9	
</p><p>
Venue: Auckland Chess Centre, 17 Cromwell Street, Mt Eden, Auckland.
<br>Format: Nine round robin, 90mins+30 secs with an extra 30mins at move 40, FIDE and NZCF rated.
The George Trundle is one of the jewels in the crown of New Zealand chess.
The luxuriant format is four individual nine round, ten player, classical round robin tournaments
with an ideal one round per day, starting at 2pm, schedule.
<br>The four tournaments are known as the Masters, Qualifiers, Reserves and Talents.
The entry fee is $100, only 40 players can be accommodated, get your entry in early.
<br>More details on the tournament website <a href="https://newzealandchess.nz/george-trundle-2021/">https://newzealandchess.nz/george-trundle-2021/</a>
<br>Normalised crosstables for this tournament will be archived in the <a href="archives-tournaments-2021.html">tournament archives</a> (so far only the Masters grade).

@snippet
@HAuckland Girls’ Chess Championship, Auckland<br>July 2nd 2021
Venue: Mt Albert War Memorial Hall, 751-761 New North Rd, Mt Albert
<br>Time 9:00 am to 2:30 pm.
<br>Format: Three separate 6 round tournaments in age groups: Over 12, Under 12 and Under 10 years.
<br>Time Control: 15 minutes plus 5 seconds per move for each player.
<br>Prizes:  Age group titles awarded for Under 18, 16, 14, 12, 10, 8, and 6 (at least 3 players required in each group for a title/medal). 
<br>Trophies and medals for place-getters, plus participation certificates for all players.
<br>This is part of an NZCF initiative to encourage girls to try chess in an all-girl environment, organised by the Waitakere Chess Club with the support of the Auckland Chess Association.
</p><p>
Download entry form <a href="downloads/Auck Girls Chess Champs 2021 entry form.pdf">here</a>.
<br>See also <a href="https://waitakerechess.co.nz/tournaments/auckland-girls-championship-2021/">
the tournament website</a>.
<br>Crosstables are available as a <a href="downloads/Auck Girls Champs 2021 Crosstables.xlsx">spreadsheet download</a> or as Swiss Perfect HTLMs for the separate sections:
<a href="downloads/Over 12 Auck Girls Champs 2021.htm">Open Section</a>, <a href="downloads/Under 12 Auck Girls Champs 2021.htm">Under 12</a>, <a href="downloads/Under 10 Auck Girls Champs 2021.htm">Under 10</a>.

@snippet
@HOtago Winter Rapid Open, Dunedin<br>June 13th 2021
The Otago Winter Rapid Open took place on Sunday 13th June with 28 players
from Otago and Southland. First place was a 4-way tie between Quentin Johnson,
Ben Suazo, Romero Suggate and Richie Christie on 4/5. The U1700 Grade was a
5-way tie on 3 points and so was the U1300 Grade on 2 points.
<br>Full results <a href="http://otagochess.org/OCCnews/news2021/wwwOtagoWinterRapidOpen2021/">here</a>.
</p><p>
Venue: Otago Chess Club, 7 Maitland Street, Dunedin.
<br>Format: 5 Round Swiss, rapid time control 25+5, NZCF rated.
<br>Tournament <a href="https://otagochess.org/tournaments.html#openrapids">website</a>.
<br>Contact: Quentin Johnson, 021 156 6789, email <a href="mailto:otagochess@gmail.com">otagochess@gmail.com</a>.
<br>Download entry form <a href="https://otagochess.org/OCCWinterRapidentryform.pdf">here</a>.

<pre>
25+10      Kuybokarov-Smirnov ½-½
25+10      Smirnov-Kuybokarov ½-½
10+10      Kuybokarov-Smirnov 0-1
10+10      Smirnov-Kuybokarov 0-1
5+3        Smirnov-Kuybokarov ½-½
5+3        Kuybokarov-Smirnov ½-½
Armageddon Kuybokarov-Smirnov 1-0
</pre>
</p><p>

move 60, Black has draw odds.

@snippet
@HOtago Autumn Rapid Open, Dunedin<br>March 7th 2021
<i>Quentin Johnson reports;</i>
<br>The Otago Autumn Rapid Open took place on Sunday 7 March and was NZCF
rated this year. This was enabled by the change in NZCF policy making
less of a barrier to casual players, who made up more than half the big
turnout of 30 players ranging from from Invercargill to Oamaru.
</p><p>
Ben Suazo of Dunedin and Atlas Kerr of Invercargill shared 1st place on
4½/5 ahead of Qi-Le Kong-Lim and Quentin Johnson both of Dunedin equal
third on 4.
</p><p>
Hamish Gold won the U1600 grade on 3½ ahead of a 4-way tie for 2nd on 3
between Julien Soler, Daniel Bell (both Invercargill), Naoki Kozakai
(Dunedin) and Greg Familton (Oamaru).
</p><p>
Corbin Fraser (invercargill) and Sen Macmaster (Oamaru) shared 1st in
the U1200 grade on 2½.
</p><p>
Full Results on Vega <a href="https://otagochess.org/OCCnews/news2021/wwwAutumnRapidOpen2021/">here</a>.
</p><p>
Venue: Otago Chess Club, 7 Maitland Street, Dunedin.
<br>Format: 5 Round Swiss, rapid time control 25+5, NZCF rated.
<br>Tournament <a href="https://otagochess.org/tournaments.html#openrapids">website</a>.
<br>Contact: Quentin Johnson, 021 156 6789, email <a href="mailto:otagochess@gmail.com">otagochess@gmail.com</a>.
<br>Download entry form <a href="https://otagochess.org/OCCAutumnRapidentryform.pdf">here</a>.

<br>Main events are 9 rounds over 9 days, plus two days of Rapid and Blitz events.

@snippet
@HKapiti Junior Chess Championship, Kapiti<br>December 12th 2020
The Kapiti Junior Chess Championship saw players
representing 22 schools from Wellington to Levin, compete across 4 divisions. In the premier Open Division,
top seed Ryan Winter (Wellington College) suffered a surprise defeat in round 1 to Josh Langford (Wellington College).
Former Paraparaumu College student, Geoffrey Gunawan, held the joint lead at the halfway stage but was not able to
carry his early momentum into the later rounds. Going into the 6th and final round, Henry Zaslow (Onslow College)
had a clear half point lead but had to settle for third place, after losing a tough battle to Kayden Loke who took
the title on tie-break, from Ryan Winter. Kayden was unbeaten throughout the tournament scoring 3 wins and 3 draws
from his 6 games.
</p><p>
Full Vega results:
<br><a href="http://kapitichess.club/tournaments/www2020-kapiti-junior-open/crosstablescore.html">Kapiti Junior Open 2020</a>
<br><a href="http://kapitichess.club/tournaments/www2020-kapiti-junior-school/rankTeams.html">Kapiti Junior (School) Chess Championship (School results)</a>
<br><a href="http://kapitichess.club/tournaments/www2020-kapiti-junior-school/rankingagegroup.html">Kapiti Junior (School) Chess Championship (Individual results by age group)</a>
</p><p>
In the School events, Vincent Lou (HIBS) was an impressive winner in the Secondary grade, with 5 points from 6,
ahead of Hamish Lester (Paraparaumu College) and Mia Vachon (Marsden Collegiate School). In the Intermediate
section, Sravya Moparthi (Hutt Intermediate) had a perfect score going into the last round, and despite a loss
playing Black against Youan Salt (Levin Intermediate), she held on to win the section on tie-break, from Youan
in second and Ryan Goodall (Levin Intermediate) taking third place. The primary section had the largest field
of all the grades and saw Lucas Qu (Churton Park) win the gold medal with silver going to Max Wang
(Johnsonville School) and bronze to William Ding (Eastern Hutt School).
</p><p>
The Kapiti Chess Club School Trophy, awarded to the top performing Kapiti Horowhenua school, was comprehensively
won by Levin Intermediate who had a strong tournament.
</p><p>
Final standings, 2020 Kapiti Junior Chess Championship:
<br>Junior Open: 1. Kayden Loke, 2. Ryan Winter (Wellington College), 3. Henry Zaslow (Onslow College)
<br>Secondary School: 1. Vincent Luo (HIBS), 2. Hamish Lester (Paraparaumu College), 3. Mia Vachon (Marsden Collegiate School)
<br>Intermediate School: 1. Sravya Moparthi (Hutt Intermediate), 2. Youan Salt (Levin Intermediate), 3. Ryan Goodall (Levin Intermediate)
<br>Primary School: 1. Lucas Qu (Churton Park), 2. Max Wang (Johnsonville School), 3. William Ding (Eastern Hutt School)
<br>Kapiti Chess Club School Trophy: Levin Intermediate (Youan Salt, Jack Davidson, Jack Grey, Ryan Goodall & Brock Clement)
</p><p>
Organised by Kapiti Club, contact is Gordon Lyall email <a href="mailto:gordon.lyall@outlook.com">gordon.lyall@outlook.com</a>.
<br>Venue: Salvation Army, rear hall, 41 Bluegum Road, Paraparaumu Beach
<br>Four six round Swiss rapid 25+5 tournaments.
<br>Entry form and more details <a href="downloads/Kapiti Junior Chess Championship 2020.pdf">here</a>.

@snippet
@HAuckland Girls’ Chess Championship, Auckland<br>November 6th 2020
Venue: Mt Albert War Memorial Hall, 751-761 New North Rd, Mt Albert
<br>Format: Three separate 6 round tournaments in age groups: Over 12, Under 12 and Under 10 years.
<br>15 minutes plus 5 seconds per move for each player.
<br>Prizes: Age group titles were awarded for Under 16, 14, 12, 10, 8, and 6. (There were insufficient players to award Under 18 titles)
<br>Trophies and medals for place-getters, plus participation certificates for all players.
</p><p>
This is part of an NZCF initiative to encourage girls to try chess in an all-girl environment run by the Waitakere Chess Club.
<br>Download entry form <a href="downloads/Auck Girls Chess Champs 2020 entry form.pdf">here (pdf)</a>.
<br>Tournament website is <a href="https://waitakerechess.co.nz/tournaments/auckland-girls-championship-2020/">here</a>.
<br>Crosstables are available as a download <a href="downloads/Auckland Girls Champs 2020 crosstables.xlsx">here</a>.
<br>147 girls took part in this year’s event.
</p><p>

@snippet
@HFIDE Online Olympiad 2020<br>August 2020
New Zealand competed at the <a href="https://olymp.fide.com/">FIDE Online Olympiad</a> on the evenings of
Friday, Saturday and Sunday 7th-9th August. We played in Division 3 Pool A, a ten team round robin and we
needed a top three placing to stay in the competition. Unfortunately we placed 7th (see crosstable below)
and were eliminated.
</p><p>
<ul>
<li>
Round by round results <a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr531770.aspx?lan=1&art=2&flag=30">here</a>
</li>
<li>
Team composition <a href="http://chess-results.com/tnr531770.aspx?lan=1&art=1&flag=30">here</a>
</li>
<li>
NZ games PGN file <a href="downloads/online-olympiad-2020.pgn">here</a>.
</li>
<li>
FIDE Online Olympiad NZ Chess Bulletin <a href="nzchessmag/interactive/2020-08.html">here</a>.
</li>
</ul>
</p>

@snippet
@HDreyer-Green Blitz Match, Auckland<br>July 18th 2020
FM Martin Dreyer played FM Ewen Green in a six game blitz match at Poppies Bookshop
Howick to celebrate FIDE's International Chess Day on July 20th #internationalchessday.
Ewen won the match 4 games to 2.
The games have been transcribed into this <a href="downloads/green-dreyer-match.pgn">PGN file</a>.
(The live link that was previously here was time limited).
</p><p>
Thanks to all involved – Paul Spiller for organizing, Ewen & Martin of course, Tony Moores for use of his shop,
Tony Booth for Arbiting, Hilton Bennett for running a book stall display, Nigel Metge for live coverage.
</p><p>
Here's an <a href="https://www.facebook.com/watch/?v=928243444311871">informative video</a> in which Paul Spiller
does his normal excellent job of explaining the wonders of chess to the general population.

@grid
images/2020/green-dreyer-match1.jpg
The match view
Let battle commence. Everyone seems happy.<br>Photo credit (all photos): Paul Spiller

@grid
images/2020/green-dreyer-match2.jpg
Noses pressed on glass
Not everyone who wanted to watch could view the action. There were some noses pressed to the glass. Arbiter
Tony Booth keeps a close watch on proceedings.

@naked
&nbsp;
&nbsp;

@grid
images/2020/green-dreyer-match3.jpg
Hilton Sells Books
It's chess! In a bookshop! Chess impresario Hilton Bennett quite rightly makes sure members of the public
are introduced to the concept of a chess book.

@grid
images/2020/green-dreyer-match4.jpg
Murray Chandler and Tony Moores
NZCF President GM Murray Chandler reaquaints himself with Poppies Bookshop proprietor Tony Moores.
Tony taught Murray at school in Wainuiomata. Believe it or not.

<br>B grade

<br>under 1400 1st Nrusingha Rath 3.5/6
<br>

<br>Under 12 1st Matthew Kangmin Kim 3/6

<br>'A' tournament for players rated 1800 and above.
<br>'B' tournament for players rated below 1800.
<br>'Junior' tournament for players aged under 20 years before 1st January 2020 and rated below 1200.
<br>The organisers reserve the right to shift a player to a different tournament if they feel an inappropriate one has been entered.
<br>Time control for all tournaments: 25 minutes + 5 second increment.
<br>Entry form <a href="downloads/BOPRapid2020.pdf">here</a>.

@snippet
@HNZ Open Championship, Tauranga<br>January 14th-22th 2020
<br>1st GM Daniel Fernandez (ENG) 8/9
<br>2nd GM Vasily Papin (RUS) 6.5/9
<br>3rd= Kirill Polishchuk, GM Darryl Johansen (AUS), IM Brandon Clarke (ENG), FM Ben Hague, IM Paul Garbett, IM Herman van Riemsdijk, IM Russell Dive 6/9
<br>Full results on <a href="tournaments/bp/2020/wwwcongress2020open/">Vega</a>.
</p><p>
A dominant performance by Daniel Fernandez winning outright by an impressive margin. His game
was the last to finish (in either grade) in the final round, and he correctly, professionally and impressively
held nothing back despite securing lone first place before the last round commenced. The
New Zealanders who made the podium are joint New Zealand Champions.
</p><p>
Rowan Wood on <a href="https://chesschat.org">ChessChat</a>:
<i>Congratulations to the NZ Champions for 2020: Kirill Polishchuk (1st win), Ben Hague (2nd win), Paul Garbett and Russell Dive (7th win).
The magic number is 6 points. Kirill drew with IM Sandler. That allowed Ben, Paul and Russell with wins over Nunilon Fulo, Noel Pinic
and Daniel Gong respectively to join him. Defending champion Anthony Ker had the uneviable task of playing tournament winner, GM Daniel
Fernandez in the last round and finished on 5.5 points in clear fifth place. GM Fernandez wins the New Zealand Open with 8 points, 1.5
points clear of GM Vasily Papin in 2nd place.</i>
</p><p>
Remarkably Paul Garbett's 7th New Zealand Championship comes 46 years after his first
in 1973/74. Russell Dive's comes a mere 33 years after his first in 1986/87! Kirill
Polishchuk's first championship caps a solid domestic season and a great tournament
with an impressive 2365 performance rating. Ben Hague's 2nd title signals a welcome
return to form, after a below par year by his lofty standards. For once Anthony Ker missed
out on a chance to improve his amazing NZ Championship statistics, but no doubt he can
take comfort from securing both NZ Rapid and Lightning titles (see below), taking revenge on GM Fernandez
in both and winning the Rapid tournament outright.

GM Daniel Fernandez from England receives his winner's cheque from NZCF president GM Murray Chandler. Photo credit <a href="https://newzealandchess.nz">NZ Chess News</a>.

Timur Gareyev and Brandon Clarke
Ben Hague, Russell Dive, Kirill Polishuck and Paul Garbett. The others have been there before, Kirill Polishchuk is rightfully thrilled to hold the Silver Rook
for the first time.

FM Bob Smith. Bob broke out some reindeer ears and a rarely seen whimsical side. Your
webmaster apologises for being the worst photographer in the world.

@snippet
@HFranklin Chess Club Results
<b>(Note that from December 2019 the Franklin Chess Club was renamed to the Counties Chess Club)</b>
<i>Ron Lanning Reports:</i>
</p><p>
The Franklin Chess club has recently travelled to test their mettle against older and stronger clubs. On
October 30th Papatoetoe (who stood down their 'A' grade players) won the match 8-2. Franklin youngsters won on
boards 1 and 3. A very enjoyable match, thanks to Stan Yee for organising. On September 8th Hamilton won
the match 10-0. Franklin had some winning and drawing chances, but sadly Hamilton were too good. Never mind
we are improving, we enjoyed the match and we look forward to the return match next year.
</p><p>
The following awards are to be made at the annual Franklin Club prizegiving.
<ul>
<li>2019 Franklin Chess Club Champion. Xavier Willoughby Ansell</li>
<li>2019 Franklin Chess Club Reserve Champion. Mark Simpson</li>
<li>2019 Franklin Chess Club Junior Champion. Benjamin Kuo</li>
<li>2019 Franklin Chess Club Most Valuable Club Member. Hemi McGrath</li>
</ul>

@HAuckland Catholic Primary Schools Chess Competition, Auckland<br>September 17th 2019
Short report by Keong Ang:
<br>135 players in 32 Teams from 11 schools participated in the 9th Auckland Catholic Primary Schools Chess Competition 2019 held at Saint Paul's School, Massey, Auckland on Tuesday 17th September 2019.
<br>
<br>The event was split into 2 tournaments, Championship and Beginners.
<br>
<br>Our Lady Star of the Sea, Howick placed 1st in both the Championship and Beginners.
<br>Saint Mary's, Northcote placed 2nd in both Championship (decided on first Game Points tiebreak) and 2nd in Beginners.
<br>Saint Paul's, Massey placed 3rd in Championship.
<br>Marist, Mount Albert placed 3rd in Beginners (decided on first Game Points tiebreak).
<br>
<br>Full details in results section of event <a href="https://chess.ac.nz/catholic2019/">webpage</a>.

@HNew Zealand Girls Interschool Championship, Auckland<br>August 8th 2019
Venue: Mt Albert War Memorial Hall, 751-761 New North Rd Mt Albert, Auckland.
<br>Format: Teams of four in three separate events – primary, intermediate an secondary
<br>Time control: 15 minutes plus 5 seconds a move
<br>
<br><b><i>Viv Smith reports</i></b>:
<br>
<br>124 girls took part in the 2019 NZ Girls Interschool Championships held on Thursday 8 August
<br>and the Mt Albert War Memorial Hall. The tournament was run by Erica Hu and Kimberley Yuan
<br>with the help of parents and the Waitakere Chess Club.
<br>
<br>Primary: (cross table <a href="downloads/Results-NZGirlsInterschoolsChess2019PRIMARY.txt">here</a>,
Vega results <a href="tournaments/misc/2019/wwwNZ Girls Primary 2019">here</a>).
<br>1st Willow Park, (Chenchen Wang, Kaylie Chen, Alexandra Shan, Sarah Sun)
<br>2nd Diocesan School for Girls, (Charlotte Ray, Lauren Ng, Sophia Liu, Bonnie Fitzgerald)
<br>3rd Hillsborough School, (Tyleah Po'e-Tofaeono, Allie O'Callaghan, Varsha Sreeram, Nitheya Anegondi)
<br>
<br>Primary Top Board Players:
<br>Board 1 Chenchen Wang, Willow Park
<br>Board 2 Lauren Ng, Diocesan School For Girls
<br>Board 3 Alexandra Shan and Sophia Liu, Willow Park and Diocesan School for Girls
<br>Board 4 Christine Injeti, Marshall Laing A
<br>
<br>Intermediate: (detailed results <a href="downloads/Results-NZGirlsInterschoolsChess2019INTERMEDIATE.txt">here</a>,
Vega results <a href="tournaments/misc/2019/wwwNZ Girls Intermediate 2019">here</a>).
<br>1st ACG Sunderland (Anya Thurner , Yolanda Chang,  Sophia Feng, Miu Miu Jin )
<br>2nd St Dominics College (Layne Almonte, Jillian Bunquin, Francesca Jones, Sophie Blomfield)
<br>3rd Glen Eden Intermediate (Gabriella Middleton, Caitlin Feasey,  Zeena Mklef,  Jasmine Barber-Gray)
<br>
<br>Intermediate Top Board Players:
<br>Board 1 Anya Thurner, ACG Sunderland
<br>Board 2 Yolanda Chang, ACG Sunderland
<br>Board 3 Francesca Jones and Sophia Feng, St Dominics College and ACG Sunderland
<br>Board 4 Jasmine Barber-Gray, Glen Eden A
<br>
<br>Secondary: (detailed results <a href="downloads/Results-NZGirlsInterschoolsChess2019SECONDARY.txt">here</a>,
Vega results <a href="tournaments/misc/2019/wwwNZ Girls Secondary 2019">here</a>).
<br>1st= Mt Roskill Grammar (Sylvia McDougall, Celia Chanwong,  Kirushni Suthakaran,  Crystal Chanwong,  Aushadhi Dharanikota)
<br>1st= Epsom Girls Grammar A (Saasha Ghadiali, Renae Ghadiali, Shriya Kelderman, Angie Zhu)
<br>3rd Westlake Girls A (Quennie Chen, Jessica Luo, Binu Kularathne, Jenny Howe)
<br>
<br><b>Note that the top three Secondary placings are determined by tie-break, and these placings were revised on 15th August after erroneous results were initially posted on 11th August.
NZCF apologises for the original error.</b> Mt Roskill Grammar and Epsom Girls Grammar have both been awarded gold medals after a recheck of the tie-break criteria.
Mt Roskill scored more game points and thus should have been declared the winners on the stated tie-break system.
Sum of opponents’ scores was used in error instead, which put Epsom Girls first on the day.
Epsom also won the direct encounter with Mt Roskill, so the organisers have decided they are also worthy winners.
<br>
<br>Secondary Top Board Players:
<br>Board 1 Sylvia McDougall, Mt Roskill Grammar
<br>Board 2 Jessica Luo, Westlake Girls A
<br>Board 3 Shriya Kelderman, Kirushni Suthakaran and Binu Kularathne, (Epsom Girls Grammar A, Mt Roskill Grammar and Westlake Girls A)
<br>Board 4 Crystal Chanwong, Mt Roskill Grammar

@snippet
@HAuckland Girls’ Chess Championship, Auckland.<br>June 28th 2019
Venue: Mt Albert War Memorial Hall, 751-761 New North Rd, Mt Albert
<br>Format: Three separate 6 round tournaments in age groups: Over 12, Under 12 and Under 10 years.
<br>15 minutes plus 5 seconds per move for each player.
<br>Prizes:  Age group titles awarded for Under 18, 16, 14, 12, 10, 8, and 6 (at least 3 players required in each group for a title/medal.)
<br>Trophies and medals for place-getters, plus participation certificates for all players.
<br>This is part of an NZCF initiative to encourage girls to try chess in an all-girl environment.
<br>
<br>

@H14th Bay of Plenty Rapid, Mt Maunganui<br>February 23rd 2019
The perennially popular event organised annually by the Mount Maunganui RSA Chess Club. This year 52 players
competed in three separate tournaments. Next year's tournament is already set for 29th Feb (easy to remember).
</p><p>
Results
<br>A-Grade
<br>1st         Romie Lord Guerra (Philippines) 5/6
<br>2nd=        FM Daniel Gong, Evan Capel (Malaysia) 4.5/6
<br>4th=        CM Alphaeus Ang, IM Russell Dive, Irmak Sipahioglu (Turkey), Ralph Hart 4/6
<br>Under 2100  Noel Pinic (Best Bay of Plenty Player) 3.5/6
<br>Under 1900  WFM Jasmine Zhang 3.5/6
<br>
<br>B-Grade (Under 1800)
<br>1st=        Chahal Aman (India), Luis Angel Duran Rubalcava (Mexico) 5/6
<br>3rd=        Timothy Ha, Simon Lyall 4/6

<br>Under 1400  Leo Kim 3/6
<br>
<br>Junior
<br>1st         Md Shahmat Mahin 6/6
<br>2nd=        Daniel Kang, Nrusingha Rath, Aidan Morgan 4/6
<br>Under 10 years old  Matthew Kim 2.5/6

@snippet
@HNZ Open Championship, Auckland.<br>January 14th-22th 2019
1st= FM Brandon Clarke (England), GM Timur Gareyev (USA) 7/9
<br>3rd= GM Vasily Papin (Russia), GM Darryl Johansen (Aus), IM Aleksandar Wohl (Aus), IM Anthony Ker,
FM Dusan Stojic (Aus), IM Russell Dive IM Leonid Sandler (Aus) 6.5/9
<br>Full results on <A HREF="tournaments/bp/2019/wwwcongress2019open/">Vega</A>.
</p><p>
As the highest placed New Zealanders, Anthony Ker and Russell Dive are joint
NZ Champions. Going into the final round Ker, Dive and Bob Smith (the usual suspects?)
were each on 5.5/8, and each faced a GM opponent in a situation where a draw was likely
sufficient for a spot on the silver rook. A special mention to Bob who got the
rough end of the draw, not only did he alone have a fifth Black, he had the strongest
and likely hungriest opponent of the three. Paul Garbett and Daniel Gong (playing each other)
and Leonard McLaren also had a chance to join Anthony and Russell, but none of these
players managed to win.
</p><p>
Anthony extends his remarkable tally of NZ championships to 14, Ortvin Sarapu's astronomical
record (20) might really be at risk. Russell's 6th title is not too shabby either.

@grid
images/2019/nzopen1a.jpg
Timur Gareyev and Brandon Clarke
The tournament winners. Timur gives a speech, Brandon reflects on three great weeks at the office.

@grid
images/2019/nzopen2a.jpg
Anthony Ker and Russell Dive
NZ Champions again, rivals and friends (with NZCF Patron Jim Benson)

@snippet
@HNZ Major Open Championship, Auckland.<br>January 14th-22th 2019
1st Romie Guerra (Phillipines) 7.5/9
<br>2nd David Lovejoy (Aus) 7/9
<br>3rd= FM Bob Gibbons and Bernd Kievelitz (Germany) 6.5/9
<br>Full results on <A HREF="tournaments/bp/2019/wwwcongress2019majoropen/">Vega</A>.
</p><p>
Unheralded (even unrated) visitor Romie Guerra wins the tournament, playing an impressive brand
of powerhouse chess. Regular visitor David Lovejoy comes second, and new NZCF
life member Bob Gibbons collects the Major Open trophy for top placing New Zealander.

@snippet
@HNZ Rapid Championship, Auckland.<br>January 23rd-24th 2019
1st GM Timur Gareyev (USA) 8.5/9
<br>2nd= GM Vasily Papin (Russia), IM Leonid Sandler (Aus), FM Brandon Clarke (England) and Ralph Hart 7.0/9
Ralph Hart as the top placing New Zealander becomes NZ Rapid champion. A special mention to new
Oceania U12 Champion (he scored 9/9 there) Sravan Renjith with a remarkable, unbeaten 6.5/9.
<br>Full results on <A HREF="tournaments/bp/2019/wwwcongress2019rapid/">Vega</A>.

@snippet
@HNZ Lightning Championship, Auckland.<br>January 24th 2019
1st GM Timur Gareyev (USA) 9/9
<br>2nd Romie Guerra (Phillipines) 7.5/9
<br>3rd Evan Capel (Malaysia) 7/9
<br>Full results on <A HREF="tournaments/bp/2019/wwwcongress2019lightning/">Vega</A>.
<br>Evan is studying in Auckland but is not a permanent resident. The top placing
New Zealanders were part of a ten way tie for =5th on 6/9. So the NZ Blitz title is
shared in by Paul Garbett, Sravan Renjith, Ralph Hart, Daniel Gong, Nigel Metge and Bob Smith.
